  148→func newClient(reg prometheus.Registerer, cfg Config, logger log.Logger) (*client, error) {\n   149→\tif cfg.URL.URL == nil {\n   150→\t\treturn nil, errors.New(\"client needs target URL\")\n 203→\tbatches := map[string]*batch{}\n   204→\n   205→\t// Given the client handles multiple batches (1 per tenant) and each batch\n   206→\t// can be created at a different point in time, we look for batches whose\n   207→\t// max wait time has been reached every 10 times per BatchWait, so that the\n   208→\t// maximum delay we have sending batches is 10% of the max waiting time.\n   209→\t// We apply a cap of 10ms to the ticker, to avoid too frequent checks in\n   210→\t// case the BatchWait is very low.\n   211→\tminWaitCheckFrequency := 10 * time.Millisecond\n   212→\tmaxWaitCheckFrequency := c.cfg.BatchWait / 10\n   213→\tif maxWaitCheckFrequency < minWaitCheckFrequency {\n   214→\t\tmaxWaitCheckFrequency = minWaitCheckFrequency\n   215→\t}\n   216→\n   217→\tmaxWaitCheck := time.NewTicker(maxWaitCheckFrequency)\n   218→\n   219→\tdefer func() {\n   220→\t\tmaxWaitCheck.Stop()\n   221→\t\t// Send all pending batches\n   222→\t\tfor tenantID, batch := range batches {\n   223→\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n   224→\t\t}\n   225→\n   226→\t\tc.wg.Done()\n   227→\t}()\n   228→\n   229→\tfor {\n   230→\t\tselect {\n   231→\t\tcase e, ok := <-c.entries:\n   232→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   233→\t\t\t\treturn\n   234→\t\t\t}\n   235→\t\t\ttenantID := c.getTenantID(e.Labels)\n   236→\t\t\tbatch, ok := batches[tenantID]\n   237→\n   238→\t\t\t// If the batch doesn't exist yet, we create a new one with the entry\n   239→\t\t\tif !ok {\n   240→\t\t\t\tbatches[tenantID] = newBatch(e)\n   241→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   242→\t\t\t}\n   243→\n   244→\t\t\t// If adding the entry to the batch will increase the size over the max\n   245→\t\t\t// size allowed, we do send the current batch and then create a new one\n   246→\t\t\tif batch.sizeBytesAfter(e) > c.cfg.BatchSize {\n   247→\t\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n   248→\n   249→\t\t\t\tbatches[tenantID] = newBatch(e)\n   250→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   251→\t\t\t}\n   252→\n   253→\t\t\t// The max size of the batch isn't reached, so we can add the entry\n   254→\t\t\tbatch.add(e)\n   255→\n   256→\t\tcase <-maxWaitCheck.C:\n   257→\t\t\t// Send all batches whose max wait time has been reached\n   258→\t\t\tfor tenantID, batch := range batches {\n   259→\t\t\t\tif batch.age() < c.cfg.BatchWait {\n   260→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   261→\t\t\t\t}\n   262→\n   263→\t\t\t\tc.sendBatch(tenantID, batch)\n   264→\t\t\t\tdelete(batches, tenantID)\n   265→\t\t\t}\n   266→\t\t}\n   267→\t}\n   268→}\n   269→\n   270→func (c *client) getTenantID(labels model.LabelSet) string {\n   271→\t// Check if it has sendBatch(tenantID string, batch *batch) {\n   291→\tbuf, entriesCount, err := batch.encode()\n   292→\tif err != nil {\n   293→\t\tc.logger.Error(\"error encoding batch\", \"error\", err)\n   294→\t\treturn\n   295→\t}\n   296→\tbufBytes := float64(len(buf))\n   297→\tc.metrics.encodedBytes.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(bufBytes)\n   298→\n   299→\tbackoff := backoff.New(c.ctx, 308→\t\t// Only retry 429s, 500s and connection-level errors.\n   309→\t\tif status > 0 && status != 429 && status/100 != 5 {\n   310→\t\t\tbreak\n   311→\t\t}\n   312→\n   313→\t\tc.logger.Warn(\"error sending batch, will retry\", \"status\", status, \"error\", err)\n   314→\t\tc.metrics.batchRetries.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Inc()\n   315→\t\tbackoff.Wait()\n   316→\n   317→\t\t// Make sure it sends at least once before checking for retry.\n   318→\t\tif !backoff.Ongoing() {\n   319→\t\t\tbreak\n   320→\t\t}\n   321→\t}\n   322→\n   323→\tif err != nil {\n   324→\t\tc.logger.Error(\"final error sending batch\", \"status\", status)\n   325→\t\tc.metrics.droppedBytes.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(bufBytes)\n   326→\t\tc.metrics.droppedEntries.WithLabelValues(c.cfg.URL.Host).Add(float64(entriesCount))\n   327→\t}\n   328→}\n   329→\n   330→func (c *client) send(ctx context.Context, tenantID string, buf 48→\tqs.Set(\"query\", query.Expr)\n    49→\n    50→\tqs.Set(\"direction\", string(query.Direction))\n    51→\n    52→\t// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,\n    53→\t// and Loki does not to parse Loki URL: %w\", err))\n    63→\t}\n    64→\n    65→\tswitch query.QueryType {\n    66→\tcase QueryTypeRange:\n    67→\t\t{\n    68→\t\t\tqs.Set(\"start\", strconv.FormatInt(query.Start.UnixNano(), 10))\n    69→\t\t\tqs.Set(\"end\", strconv.FormatInt(query.End.UnixNano(), 10))\n    70→\t\t\t// NOTE: technically for streams-producing queries `step`\n    71→\t\t\t// is ignored, so it would be nicer to not send it in such cases,\n    72→\t\t\t// but we cannot detect that situation, so we always send it.\n    73→\t\t\t// it should not break anything.\n    74→\t\t\t// NOTE2: we do this at millisecond precision for two reasons:\n    75→\t\t\t//  a. Loki cannot do steps with better precision anyway,\n    76→\t\t\t//     so the microsecond & nanosecond part can be ignored.\n    77→\t\t\t//  b. having it always be number+'ms' makes it more robust 85→\t\t\tqs.Set(\"time\", strconv.FormatInt(query.End.UnixNano(), 10))\n    86→\t\t\tlokiUrl.Path = path.Join(lokiUrl.Path, \"/loki/api/v1/query\")\n    87→\t\t}\n    88→\tdefault:\n    89→\t\treturn 106→\tsetXScopeOrgIDHeader(req, ctx)\n   107→\n   108→\treturn req, nil\n   109→}\n   110→\n   111→type lokiResponseError struct {\n   112→\tMessage string `json:\"message\"`\n   113→\tTraceID string `json:\"traceID,omitempty\"`\n   114→}\n   115→\n   116→type lokiError struct {\n   117→\tMessage string\n   118→}\n   119→\n   120→func makeLokiError(bytes []byte) error {\n   121→\tvar data lokiError\n   122→\terr := json.Unmarshal(bytes, &data)\n   123→\tif err != nil {\n   124→\t\t// we were unable to convert the bytes to JSON, we return the whole text\n   125→\t\treturn 143→\t\treturn err\n   144→\t}\n   145→\n   146→\tbytes := buf.Bytes()\n   147→\n   148→\t// the error-message is probably a JSON structure,\n   149→\t// with a string-field named \"message\". we want 154→\t// - we try to convert the bytes to JSON\n   155→\t// - we take the value of the field \"message\"\n   156→\t// - if any of these steps fail, or if \"message\" is empty, we return the whole 154→\t// - we try to convert the bytes to JSON\n   155→\t// - we take the value of the field \"message\"\n   156→\t// - if any of these steps fail, or if \"message\" is empty, we return the whole 271→}\n   272→\n   273→// we extracted this part of the functionality to make it easy to unit-test it\n   274→func runQuery(ctx context.Context, api *LokiAPI, query *lokiQuery, responseOpts getSupportingQueryHeaderValue(supportingQueryType SupportingQueryType) string {\n   322→\tvalue := \"\"\n   323→\n   324→\t// we need to map the SupportingQueryType to the actual header value. Here are the key findings:\n\n## Instant Query Endpoint (`/loki/api/v1/query`)\n\nThe `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint allows for doing queries against a single point in time, often referred to as an instant query.\n\n## Query Constraints\n\nInstant queries are only used for metric type LogQL queries and will return a 400 (Bad Request) in case a log type query is provided.\n\n## Query Parameters\n\nThe endpoint accepts query parameters including: the LogQL query to perform, the evaluation time for the query as a nanosecond Unix epoch or another supported format (defaulting to now), and direction parameters that determine the sort order of logs (supporting values of forward or backward, defaulting to backward).\n\n## Recent API Changes\n\nA recent update changed the behavior of the instant query endpoint so that it no longer allows log selector expressions, instead returning a 400 (Bad Request) with the error message \"log queries are not supported as an instant query type, please change you query to a range query type\".\n\nIn microservices mode, `/loki/api/v1/query` is exposed by the querier and the query frontend.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown
